did a lot for my career personally. It gave me an opportunity to revisit the times where that cream meant that much to us. So, yeah, when I think of this record it just automatically puts me back into ‘87/’88 where we were standing in front of the building. It’s cold outside. We didn’t care. We’re out there, all black on trying to make dollars. Just trying to make some money and trying to eat. Survive.&lt;/p&gt;\n\n&lt;p&gt;This song, I remember writing to the beat a long time ago before we actually came out. That beat is old. That was probably like a ‘89 beat. RZA had it that long because he had a bunch of breaks. He had all kind of things and he was making beats back then, but we was just picking and that beat happened to always sit around and I would be like, ‘I want that beat, so don’t give that beat to nobody.’ And he kept his word and let me have it.&lt;/p&gt;\n\n&lt;p&gt;Meth came up with the hook but our dude named Raider Ruckus, this was like Meth’s homeboy back then, like they was real close, he came up with the phrase ‘cash rules everything around me.’ So when he showed Meth what it was and was like, ‘Cash rules everything around me,’ Meth was like, ‘Word, you right!’ And turned it into a movie, and I came in later that day and heard it and co-signed it.&lt;/p&gt;\n&lt;/blockquote&gt;\n\n&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=\&quot;http://www.complex.com/music/2011/03/raekwon-25-essential-songs/cream\&quot; rel=\&quot;noopener nofollow\&quot;&gt;via Complex&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&quot;,&quot;markdown&quot;:&quot;&gt; ‘C.R.E.A.M.’ did a lot for my career personally. It gave me an opportunity to revisit the times where that cream meant that much to us. So, yeah, when I think of this record it just automatically puts me back into ‘87/’88 where we were standing in front of the building. It’s cold outside. We didn’t care. We’re out there, all black on trying to make dollars. Just trying to make some money and trying to eat. Survive.\n\n&gt; This song, I remember writing to the beat a long time ago before we actually came out. That beat is old. That was probably like a ‘89 beat. RZA had it that long because he had a bunch of breaks. He had all kind of things and he was making beats back then, but we was just picking and that beat happened to always sit around and I would be like, ‘I want that beat, so don’t give that beat to nobody.’ And he kept his word and let me have it.\n\n&gt; Meth came up with the hook but our dude named Raider Ruckus, this was like Meth’s homeboy back then, like they was real close, he came up with the phrase ‘cash rules everything around me.’ So when he showed Meth what it was and was like, ‘Cash rules everything around me,’ Meth was like, ‘Word, you right!’ And turned it into a movie, and I came in later that day and heard it and co-signed it.\n\n[via Complex](http://www.complex.com/music/2011/03/raekwon-25-essential-songs/cream)&quot;},&quot;created_at&quot;:1523776847,&quot;editorial_state&quot;:&quot;normal&quot;,&quot;has_voters&quot;:true,&quot;id&quot;:107662,&quot;votes_total&quot;:5,&quot;current_user_metadata&quot;:{&quot;permissions&quot;:[&quot;vote&quot;],&quot;excluded_permissions&quot;:[&quot;edit&quot;,&quot;destroy&quot;],&quot;interactions&quot;:{&quot;vote&quot;:null}},&quot;answer_source&quot;:null,&quot;authors&quot;:[{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;user_attribution&quot;,&quot;attribution&quot;:1.0,&quot;pinned_role&quot;:null,&quot;user&quot;:{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;user&quot;,&quot;about_me_summary&quot;:&quot;Hi all. is a true song. Everything Inspectah Deck and Raekwon said is 100 percent true. Not one line in that entire song is a lie, or even a slight exaggeration. Deck did sell base, and he did go to jail at the age of fifteen. Rae was sticking up white boys on ball courts, rocking the same damn ’Lo sweater. And of “course, Meth on the hook was like butter on the popcorn. Meth knew the hard times, too, being out there smoking woolies and pumping crack, etc. That raspy shit he was kicking just echoed in everyone’s head long after the song was done playing.&lt;br&gt;&lt;br&gt;The realism on “C.R.E.A.M.” is what resonates with so many people all over the world. People everywhere know that sentiment of being slaves to the dollar. Cash is king, and we are its lowly subjects. That’s pretty much the case in every nation around the world, the desperation to put your life and your freedom on the line to make a couple dollars. Whether you’re working, stripping, hustling, or slinging, whether you’re a business owner or homeless, cash rules everything around us.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;\n\n&lt;p&gt;Source:  &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36341538-raw\&quot; rel=\&quot;noopener nofollow\&quot;&gt;Raw:My Journey into Wu-Tang&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&quot;,&quot;markdown&quot;:&quot;&gt;“C.R.E.A.M.” is a true song. Everything Inspectah Deck and Raekwon said is 100 percent true. Not one line in that entire song is a lie, or even a slight exaggeration. Deck did sell base, and he did go to jail at the age of fifteen. Rae was sticking up white boys on ball courts, rocking the same damn ’Lo sweater. And of “course, Meth on the hook was like butter on the popcorn. Meth knew the hard times, too, being out there smoking woolies and pumping crack, etc. That raspy shit he was kicking just echoed in everyone’s head long after the song was done playing.&lt;br&gt;&lt;/br&gt;&lt;br&gt;&lt;/br&gt;The realism on “C.R.E.A.M.” is what resonates with so many people all over the world. People everywhere know that sentiment of being slaves to the dollar. Cash is king, and we are its lowly subjects. That’s pretty much the case in every nation around the world, the desperation to put your life and your freedom on the line to make a couple dollars. Whether you’re working, stripping, hustling, or slinging, whether you’re a business owner or homeless, cash rules everything around us.\n\nSource:  [Raw:My Journey into has Method Man said about the song?&quot;,&quot;contributors_count&quot;:1,&quot;created_at&quot;:1568676370,&quot;default_key&quot;:null,&quot;has_voters&quot;:false,&quot;id&quot;:453029,&quot;pin_order&quot;:327680.0,&quot;state&quot;:&quot;pinned&quot;,&quot;url&quot;:&quot;https://genius.com/Wu-tang-clan-cream-lyrics/questions/453029&quot;,&quot;votes_total&quot;:0,&quot;current_user_metadata&quot;:{&quot;permissions&quot;:[&quot;vote&quot;],&quot;excluded_permissions&quot;:[&quot;add_answer&quot;,&quot;update_answer_source&quot;,&quot;edit&quot;,&quot;archive&quot;,&quot;pin&quot;,&quot;unpin&quot;,&quot;move&quot;,&quot;add_verified_answer&quot;],&quot;iq_by_action&quot;:{&quot;answer&quot;:{&quot;primary&quot;:{&quot;multiplier&quot;:1,&quot;base&quot;:5.0,&quot;applicable&quot;:true},&quot;pin&quot;:{&quot;multiplier&quot;:1,&quot;base&quot;:5.0,&quot;applicable&quot;:true}},&quot;archive&quot;:{&quot;primary&quot;:{&quot;multiplier&quot;:1,&quot;base&quot;:1.0,&quot;applicable&quot;:true}}},&quot;interactions&quot;:{&quot;vote&quot;:null}},&quot;answer&quot;:{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;answer&quot;,&quot;body&quot;:{&quot;html&quot;:&quot;&lt;p&gt;Meth &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.complex.com/music/2011/10/method-man-25-essential-songs/wu-tang-clan-cream-1993\&quot; rel=\&quot;noopener nofollow\&quot;&gt;told &lt;em&gt;Complex&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt;,&lt;/p&gt;\n\n&lt;blockquote&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;‘C.R.E.A.M.’ was the one that really put us on the map if you wanna be technical. I wasn’t there when they recorded ‘C.R.E.A.M.’ I came in after the fact. RZA was like, ‘Put a hook on this song’ and I put a hook on it. That’s how it always went. I liked doing hooks.&lt;/p&gt;\n\n&lt;p&gt;The hook for that was done by my man Raider Ruckus. We used to work at the Statue of Liberty and when we were coming home we used to come up with all these made-up words that were acronyms.&lt;/p&gt;\n\n&lt;p&gt;We had words like ‘BIBWAM’ which meant, ‘Bitches Is Busted Without A Man’ and all this other crazy shit. Raider Ruckus was so ill with the way he put the words together. We would call money ‘cream’ so he took each letter and made a word out of it and killed it the way he did it.&lt;/p&gt;\n\n&lt;p&gt;Something like that had never been done before as far as a hook or even a way of speaking. This is just showing and proving that we paid attention in class when we was kids. You can’t do shit like that unless you got a brain in your fucking head! You got to have some level of intelligence to do something like that.&lt;/p&gt;\n\n&lt;p&gt;The best acronym for a word that I heard was ‘P.R.O.J.E.C.T.S.’ by Killah Priest. He said ‘People Relying On Just Enough Cash To Survive.’ And he’s the one that came up with ‘Basic Instructions Before Leaving Earth,’ the acronym for B.I.B.L.E. This ain’t no fluke shit man.&lt;/p&gt;\n\n&lt;p&gt;There’s a reason you got millions upon millions of fucking kids running around with Wu-Tang tattoos. You don’t just put something on your body permanently unless it’s official. At that time, when you’re coming out brand new and representing where you come from, everybody from that area wants you to win because they win. That’s what it was like for us.&lt;/p&gt;\n\n&lt;p&gt;We were the only dudes from Staten Island doing it so everybody from Staten Island wanted us to win. Not just dudes from Staten Island, but dudes from Brooklyn too because they had peoples in the group too. Then it was just grimy niggas who loved to see real shit, saying, ‘We riding with them Wu-Tang niggas. Fuck all that shiny suit shit!’ That ain’t no take on Puff, a lot of niggas was wearing suits and shit man, but that ain’t us.&lt;/p&gt;\n&lt;/blockquote&gt;&quot;,&quot;markdown&quot;:&quot;Meth [told *Complex*](https://www.complex.com/music/2011/10/method-man-25-essential-songs/wu-tang-clan-cream-1993),\n\n&gt;‘C.R.E.A.M.’ was the one that really put us on the map if you wanna be technical. I wasn’t there when they recorded ‘C.R.E.A.M.’ I came in after the fact. RZA was like, ‘Put a hook on this song’ and I put a hook on it. That’s how it always went. I liked doing hooks.\n\n&gt;The hook for that was done by my man Raider Ruckus. We used to work at the Statue of Liberty and when we were coming home we used to come up with all these made-up words that were acronyms.\n\n&gt;We had words like ‘BIBWAM’ which meant, ‘Bitches Is Busted Without A Man’ and all this other crazy shit. Raider Ruckus was so ill with the way he put the words together. We would call money ‘cream’ so he took each letter and made a word out of it and killed it the way he did it.\n\n&gt;Something like that had never been done before as far as a hook or even a way of speaking. This is just showing and proving that we paid attention in class when we was kids. You can’t do shit like that unless you got a brain in your fucking head! You got to have some level of intelligence to do something like that.\n\n&gt;The best acronym for a word that I heard was ‘P.R.O.J.E.C.T.S.’ by Killah Priest. He said ‘People Relying On Just Enough Cash To Survive.’ And he’s the one that came up with ‘Basic Instructions Before Leaving Earth,’ the acronym for B.I.B.L.E. This ain’t no fluke shit man.\n\n&gt;There’s a reason you got millions upon millions of fucking kids running around with Wu-Tang tattoos. You don’t just put something on your body permanently unless it’s official. At that time, when you’re coming out brand new and representing where you come from, everybody from that area wants you to win because they win. That’s what it was like for us.\n\n&gt;We were the only dudes from Staten Island doing it so everybody from Staten Island wanted us to win. Not just dudes from Staten Island, but dudes from Brooklyn too because they had peoples in the group too. The timeless piano riffs and background vocals come from a chopped up sample of &lt;a href=\&quot;https://genius.com/artists/The-charmels\&quot; rel=\&quot;noopener\&quot; data-api_path=\&quot;/artists/100350\&quot;&gt;The Charmels&lt;/a&gt;‘ 1967 record, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://genius.com/The-charmels-as-long-as-ive-got-you-lyrics\&quot; rel=\&quot;noopener\&quot; data-api_path=\&quot;/songs/279344\&quot;&gt;“As Long As I’ve Got You,”&lt;/a&gt; that make up the entire track.&lt;/p&gt;\n\n&lt;p&gt;Although it was released as an official single in 1994, “C.R.E.A.M.” was &lt;a href=\&quot;https://youtu.be/yrQPCKSWZmI?t=219\&quot; rel=\&quot;noopener nofollow\&quot;&gt;first recorded&lt;/a&gt; in 1991, around the same time as RZA’s &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.pghcitypaper.com/pittsburgh/wu-tangs-rza-found-his-second-chance-in-steubenville/Content?oid=1637802\&quot; rel=\&quot;noopener nofollow\&quot;&gt;assault case&lt;/a&gt;, and featured himself and Ghostface Killah. The track went through several revisions and was later re-recorded by Raekwon and Inspectah Deck in 1993—an &lt;a href=\&quot;https://ambrosiaforheads.com/2017/09/wu-tang-clan-logo-history-rza/\&quot; rel=\&quot;noopener nofollow\&quot;&gt;early title&lt;/a&gt; of the song was “Lifestyles of the Mega-Rich.”&lt;/p&gt;\n\n&lt;p&gt;In 2017, RZA &lt;a href=\&quot;https://youtu.be/yrQPCKSWZmI?t=188\&quot; rel=\&quot;noopener nofollow\&quot;&gt;explained to &lt;em&gt;Power 106&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt; how the final version of the track came together:&lt;/p&gt;\n\n&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;Once we got to the studio, I decided that this track had to be on the Wu-Tang album. I reminded Rae and Deck of their verses—their verses were long. […] Method Man, the master of hooks at the time, came in with this hook right here: ‘cash rules everything around me, cream, get the money.’ Once he added that element, I knew it was going to be a smash.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;\n\n&lt;p&gt;Since its release, the song and chorus have been &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.whosampled.com/Wu-Tang-Clan/C.R.E.A.M./\&quot; rel=\&quot;noopener nofollow\&quot;&gt;referenced countless times&lt;/a&gt; by several artists. It has also been featured in movies such as &lt;a href=\&quot;https://genius.com/artists/Eminem\&quot; rel=\&quot;noopener\&quot; data-api_path=\&quot;/artists/45\&quot;&gt;Eminem&lt;/a&gt;’s &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.imdb.com/title/tt0298203/\&quot; rel=\&quot;noopener nofollow\&quot;&gt;&lt;em&gt;8 Mile&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt; and the &lt;a href=\&quot;https://genius.com/artists/Nwa\&quot; rel=\&quot;noopener\&quot; data-api_path=\&quot;/artists/974\&quot;&gt;N.W.A&lt;/a&gt; biopic, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.imdb.com/title/tt01398426/\&quot; rel=\&quot;noopener nofollow\&quot;&gt;&lt;em&gt;Straight Outta Compton&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;,&quot;markdown&quot;:&quot;Arguably one of the most [iconic songs in hip-hop](https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-lists/the-50-greatest-hip-hop-songs-of-all-time-150547/wu-tang-clan-c-r-e-a-m-96125/), the underlying idea of “C.R.E.A.M.” is found in its title---[cash rules everything](https://genius.com/1741691). The timeless piano riffs and background vocals come from a chopped up sample of [The Charmels](https://genius.com/artists/The-charmels)&#39; 1967 record, [\&quot;As Long As I&#39;ve Got You,\&quot;](https://genius.com/The-charmels-as-long-as-ive-got-you-lyrics) that make up the entire track. \n\nAlthough it was released as an official single in 1994, “C.R.E.A.M.” was [first recorded](https://youtu.be/yrQPCKSWZmI?t=219) in 1991, around the same time as RZA’s [assault case](https://www.pghcitypaper.com/pittsburgh/wu-tangs-rza-found-his-second-chance-in-steubenville/Content?oid=1637802), and featured himself and Ghostface Killah. The track went through several revisions and was later re-recorded by Raekwon and Inspectah Deck in 1993---an [early title](https://ambrosiaforheads.com/2017/09/wu-tang-clan-logo-history-rza/) of the song was “Lifestyles of the Mega-Rich.” \n\nIn 2017, RZA [explained to *Power 106*](https://youtu.be/yrQPCKSWZmI?t=188) how the final version of the track came together: \n\n&gt; Once we got to the studio, I decided that this track had to be on the Wu-Tang album. I reminded Rae and Deck of their verses---their verses were long. […] Method Man, the master of hooks at the time, came in with this hook right here: ‘cash rules everything around me, cream, get the money.’ Once he added that element, I knew it was going to be a smash. \n\nSince its release, the song and chorus have been [referenced countless times](https://www.whosampled.com/Wu-Tang-Clan/C.R.E.A.M./) by several artists. It has also been featured in movies such as [Eminem](https://genius.com/artists/Eminem)&#39;s [*8 Mile*](https://www.imdb.com/title/tt0298203/) and the [N.W.A](https://genius.com/artists/Nwa) biopic, [*Straight Outta Compton*](https://www.imdb.com/title/tt01398426/).&quot;},&quot;description_preview&quot;:&quot;Arguably one of the most iconic songs in hip-hop, the underlying idea of “C.R.E.A.M.” is found in its title—cash rules everything. The timeless piano riffs and background vocals come from a chopped up sample of The Charmels‘ 1967 record, “As Long As I’ve Got You,” that make up the entire track.\n\nAlthough it was released as an official single in 1994, “C.R.E.A.M.” was first recorded in 1991, around the same time as RZA’s assault case, and featured himself and Ghostface Killah. The track went through several revisions and was later re-recorded by Raekwon and Inspectah Deck in 1993—an early title of the song was “Lifestyles of the Mega-Rich.”\n\nIn 2017, RZA explained to Power 106 how the final version of the track came \n\nOnce we got to the studio, I decided that this track had to be on the Wu-Tang album. I reminded Rae and Deck of their verses—their verses were long. […] Method Man, the master of hooks at the time, came in with this hook right  ‘cash rules everything around me, cream, get the money.’ Once he added that element, I knew it was going to be a smash.\n\nSince its release, the song and chorus have been referenced countless times by several artists. Clan&quot;,&quot;id&quot;:28,&quot;image_url&quot;:&quot;https://images.genius.com/d6fca15fbb1e4624835e01e64a6b59c4.1000x1000x1.jpg&quot;,&quot;link_title&quot;:&quot;C.R.E.A.M. by Wu-Tang Clan&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;C.R.E.A.M.&quot;,&quot;type&quot;:&quot;Song&quot;,&quot;url&quot;:&quot;https://genius.com/Wu-tang-clan-cream-lyrics&quot;},&quot;annotations&quot;:[{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;annotation&quot;,&quot;api_path&quot;:&quot;/annotations/3489772&quot;,&quot;being_created&quot;:false,&quot;body&quot;:{&quot;html&quot;:&quot;&lt;p&gt;Arguably one of the most &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-lists/the-50-greatest-hip-hop-songs-of-all-time-150547/wu-tang-clan-c-r-e-a-m-96125/\&quot; rel=\&quot;noopener nofollow\&quot;&gt;iconic songs in hip-hop&lt;/a&gt;, the underlying idea of “C.R.E.A.M.” is found in its title—&lt;a href=\&quot;https://genius.com/1741691\&quot; rel=\&quot;noopener\&quot; data-api_path=\&quot;/referents/1741691\&quot;&gt;cash rules everything&lt;/a&gt;. The timeless piano riffs and background vocals come from a chopped up sample of &lt;a href=\&quot;https://genius.com/artists/The-charmels\&quot; rel=\&quot;noopener\&quot; data-api_path=\&quot;/artists/100350\&quot;&gt;The Charmels&lt;/a&gt;‘ 1967 record, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://genius.com/The-charmels-as-long-as-ive-got-you-lyrics\&quot; rel=\&quot;noopener\&quot; data-api_path=\&quot;/songs/279344\&quot;&gt;“As Long As I’ve Got You,”&lt;/a&gt; that make up the entire track.&lt;/p&gt;\n\n&lt;p&gt;Although it was released as an official single in 1994, “C.R.E.A.M.” was &lt;a href=\&quot;https://youtu.be/yrQPCKSWZmI?t=219\&quot; rel=\&quot;noopener nofollow\&quot;&gt;first recorded&lt;/a&gt; in 1991, around the same time as RZA’s &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.pghcitypaper.com/pittsburgh/wu-tangs-rza-found-his-second-chance-in-steubenville/Content?oid=1637802\&quot; rel=\&quot;noopener nofollow\&quot;&gt;assault case&lt;/a&gt;, and featured himself and Ghostface Killah. The track went through several revisions and was later re-recorded by Raekwon and Inspectah Deck in 1993—an &lt;a href=\&quot;https://ambrosiaforheads.com/2017/09/wu-tang-clan-logo-history-rza/\&quot; rel=\&quot;noopener nofollow\&quot;&gt;early title&lt;/a&gt; of the song was “Lifestyles of the Mega-Rich.”&lt;/p&gt;\n\n&lt;p&gt;In 2017, RZA &lt;a href=\&quot;https://youtu.be/yrQPCKSWZmI?t=188\&quot; rel=\&quot;noopener nofollow\&quot;&gt;explained to &lt;em&gt;Power 106&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt; how the final version of the track came together:&lt;/p&gt;\n\n&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;Once we got to the studio, I decided that this track had to be on the Wu-Tang album. I reminded Rae and Deck of their verses—their verses were long. […] Method Man, the master of hooks at the time, came in with this hook right here: ‘cash rules everything around me, cream, get the money.’ Once he added that element, I knew it was going to be a smash.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;\n\n&lt;p&gt;Since its release, the song and chorus have been &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.whosampled.com/Wu-Tang-Clan/C.R.E.A.M./\&quot; rel=\&quot;noopener nofollow\&quot;&gt;referenced countless times&lt;/a&gt; by several artists. It has also been featured in movies such as &lt;a href=\&quot;https://genius.com/artists/Eminem\&quot; rel=\&quot;noopener\&quot; data-api_path=\&quot;/artists/45\&quot;&gt;Eminem&lt;/a&gt;’s &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.imdb.com/title/tt0298203/\&quot; rel=\&quot;noopener nofollow\&quot;&gt;&lt;em&gt;8 Mile&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt; and the &lt;a href=\&quot;https://genius.com/artists/Nwa\&quot; rel=\&quot;noopener\&quot; data-api_path=\&quot;/artists/974\&quot;&gt;N.W.A&lt;/a&gt; biopic, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.imdb.com/title/tt01398426/\&quot; rel=\&quot;noopener nofollow\&quot;&gt;&lt;em&gt;Straight Outta Compton&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;,&quot;markdown&quot;:&quot;Arguably one of the most [iconic songs in hip-hop](https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-lists/the-50-greatest-hip-hop-songs-of-all-time-150547/wu-tang-clan-c-r-e-a-m-96125/), the underlying idea of “C.R.E.A.M.” is found in its title---[cash rules everything](https://genius.com/1741691). The timeless piano riffs and background vocals come from a chopped up sample of [The Charmels](https://genius.com/artists/The-charmels)&#39; 1967 record, [\&quot;As Long As I&#39;ve Got You,\&quot;](https://genius.com/The-charmels-as-long-as-ive-got-you-lyrics) that make up the entire track. \n\nAlthough it was released as an official single in 1994, “C.R.E.A.M.” was [first recorded](https://youtu.be/yrQPCKSWZmI?t=219) in 1991, around the same time as RZA’s [assault case](https://www.pghcitypaper.com/pittsburgh/wu-tangs-rza-found-his-second-chance-in-steubenville/Content?oid=1637802), and featured himself and Ghostface Killah. The track went through several revisions and was later re-recorded by Raekwon and Inspectah Deck in 1993---an [early title](https://ambrosiaforheads.com/2017/09/wu-tang-clan-logo-history-rza/) of the song was “Lifestyles of the Mega-Rich.” \n\nIn 2017, RZA [explained to *Power 106*](https://youtu.be/yrQPCKSWZmI?t=188) how the final version of the track came together: \n\n&gt; Once we got to the studio, I decided that this track had to be on the Wu-Tang album. I reminded Rae and Deck of their verses---their verses were long. […] Method Man, the master of hooks at the time, came in with this hook right here: ‘cash rules everything around me, cream, get the money.’ Once he added that element, I knew it was going to be a smash. \n\nSince its release, the song and chorus have been [referenced countless times](https://www.whosampled.com/Wu-Tang-Clan/C.R.E.A.M./) by several artists. It has also been featured in movies such as [Eminem](https://genius.com/artists/Eminem)&#39;s [*8 Mile*](https://www.imdb.com/title/tt0298203/) and the [N.W.A](https://genius.com/artists/Nwa) biopic, [*Straight Outta Compton*](https://www.imdb.com/title/tt01398426/).&quot;},&quot;comment_count&quot;:0,&quot;community&quot;:true,&quot;created_at&quot;:1254082240,&quot;custom_preview&quot;:null,&quot;deleted&quot;:false,&quot;embed_content&quot;:&quot;&lt;blockquote   <div class="column_layout-column_span column_layout-column_span--secondary u-top_margin column_layout-flex_column">
    <div class="column_layout-column_span-initial_content">
      
        
      

      <div class="annotation_label">
        
          <h3 class="u-inline">
            About “C.R.E.A.M.”
          </h3>
        
        
      </div>
      <div class="rich_text_formatting">
        <p>Arguably one of the most <a href="https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-lists/the-50-greatest-hip-hop-songs-of-all-time-150547/wu-tang-clan-c-r-e-a-m-96125/" rel="noopener nofollow">iconic songs in hip-hop</a>, the underlying idea of “C.R.E.A.M.” is found in its title—<a href="https://genius.com/1741691" rel="noopener" data-api_path="/referents/1741691">cash rules everything</a>. The timeless piano riffs and background vocals come from a chopped up sample of <a href="https://genius.com/artists/The-charmels" rel="noopener" data-api_path="/artists/100350">The Charmels</a>‘ 1967 record, <a href="https://genius.com/The-charmels-as-long-as-ive-got-you-lyrics" rel="noopener" data-api_path="/songs/279344">“As Long As I’ve Got You,”</a> that make up the entire track.</p>

<p>Although it was released as an official single in 1994, “C.R.E.A.M.” was <a href="https://youtu.be/yrQPCKSWZmI?t=219" rel="noopener nofollow">first recorded</a> in 1991, around the same time as RZA’s <a href="https://www.pghcitypaper.com/pittsburgh/wu-tangs-rza-found-his-second-chance-in-steubenville/Content?oid=1637802" rel="noopener nofollow">assault case</a>, and featured himself and Ghostface Killah. The track went through several revisions and was later re-recorded by Raekwon and Inspectah Deck in 1993—an <a href="https://ambrosiaforheads.com/2017/09/wu-tang-clan-logo-history-rza/" rel="noopener nofollow">early title</a> of the song was “Lifestyles of the Mega-Rich.”</p>

<p>In 2017, RZA <a href="https://youtu.be/yrQPCKSWZmI?t=188" rel="noopener nofollow">explained to <em>Power 106</em></a> how the final version of the track came together:</p>

<blockquote><p>Once we got to the studio, I decided that this track had to be on the Wu-Tang album. I reminded Rae and Deck of their verses—their verses were long. […] Method Man, the master of hooks at the time, came in with this hook right here: ‘cash rules everything around me, cream, get the money.’ Once he added that element, I knew it was going to be a smash.</p></blockquote>

<p>Since its release, the song and chorus have been <a href="https://www.whosampled.com/Wu-Tang-Clan/C.R.E.A.M./" rel="noopener nofollow">referenced countless times</a> by several artists. It has also been featured in movies such as <a href="https://genius.com/artists/Eminem" rel="noopener" data-api_path="/artists/45">Eminem</a>’s <a href="https://www.imdb.com/title/tt0298203/" rel="noopener nofollow"><em>8 Mile</em></a> and the <a href="https://genius.com/artists/Nwa" rel="noopener" data-api_path="/artists/974">N.W.A</a> biopic, <a href="https://www.imdb.com/title/tt01398426/" rel="noopener nofollow"><em>Straight Outta Compton</em></a>.</p>
      </div>
      <div class="song_metadata u-xx_large_bottom_margin"></div>
    </div>

    <div class="column_layout-column_span-initial_content">
      <div initial-content-for="question_list">
  <ul>
    
      <li  class="question question--bottom_border ">
  <div class="u-bottom_margin">
    <h3 class="annotation_label">What has RZA said about the song?</h3>
  </div>
  
  <div class="rich_text_formatting rich_text_formatting--no_vertical_margins">
    <p></p><div class="embedly_preview embedly_preview--video">
<iframe type="text/html" width="640" height="390" frameborder="0" allowfullscreen="1" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/yrQPCKSWZmI?modestbranding=1&amp;start=187&amp;showinfo=0&amp;enablejsapi=1&amp;origin=genius.com"></iframe>
</div>
  </div>


</li>

    
      <li  class="question question--bottom_border ">
  <div class="u-bottom_margin">
    <h3 class="annotation_label">What has Raekwon said about the song?</h3>
  </div>
  
  <div class="rich_text_formatting rich_text_formatting--no_vertical_margins">
    <blockquote>
<p>‘C.R.E.A.M.’ did a lot for my career personally. It gave me an opportunity to revisit the times where that cream meant that much to us. So, yeah, when I think of this record it just automatically puts me back into ‘87/’88 where we were standing in front of the building. It’s cold outside. We didn’t care. We’re out there, all black on trying to make dollars. Just trying to make some money and trying to eat. Survive.</p>

<p>This song, I remember writing to the beat a long time ago before we actually came out. That beat is old. That was probably like a ‘89 beat. RZA had it that long because he had a bunch of breaks. He had all kind of things and he was making beats back then, but we was just picking and that beat happened to always sit around and I would be like, ‘I want that beat, so don’t give that beat to nobody.’ And he kept his word and let me have it.</p>

<p>Meth came up with the hook but our dude named Raider Ruckus, this was like Meth’s homeboy back then, like they was real close, he came up with the phrase ‘cash rules everything around me.’ So when he showed Meth what it was and was like, ‘Cash rules everything around me,’ Meth was like, ‘Word, you right!’ And turned it into a movie, and I came in later that day and heard it and co-signed it.</p>
</blockquote>

<p><a href="http://www.complex.com/music/2011/03/raekwon-25-essential-songs/cream" rel="noopener nofollow">via Complex</a></p>
  </div>


</li>

    
      <li  class="question question--bottom_border ">
  <div class="u-bottom_margin">
    <h3 class="annotation_label">What has U-God said about the song?</h3>
  </div>
  
  <div class="rich_text_formatting rich_text_formatting--no_vertical_margins">
    <blockquote><p>“C.R.E.A.M.” is a true song. Everything Inspectah Deck and Raekwon said is 100 percent true. Not one line in that entire song is a lie, or even a slight exaggeration. Deck did sell base, and he did go to jail at the age of fifteen. Rae was sticking up white boys on ball courts, rocking the same damn ’Lo sweater. And of “course, Meth on the hook was like butter on the popcorn. Meth knew the hard times, too, being out there smoking woolies and pumping crack, etc. That raspy shit he was kicking just echoed in everyone’s head long after the song was done playing.<br><br>The realism on “C.R.E.A.M.” is what resonates with so many people all over the world. People everywhere know that sentiment of being slaves to the dollar. Cash is king, and we are its lowly subjects. That’s pretty much the case in every nation around the world, the desperation to put your life and your freedom on the line to make a couple dollars. Whether you’re working, stripping, hustling, or slinging, whether you’re a business owner or homeless, cash rules everything around us.</p></blockquote>

<p>Source:  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36341538-raw" rel="noopener nofollow">Raw:My Journey into Wu-Tang</a></p>
  </div>


</li>

    
      <li  class="question question--bottom_border ">
  <div class="u-bottom_margin">
    <h3 class="annotation_label">What songs were sampled on the beat for “C.R.E.A.M.?”</h3>
  </div>
  
  <div class="rich_text_formatting rich_text_formatting--no_vertical_margins">
    <p>The vocals and background sample that can be heard on the song’s intro were taken taken from <a href="https://genius.com/artists/The-charmels" rel="noopener" data-api_path="/artists/100350">The Charmels</a>’ 1967 song <a href="https://genius.com/The-charmels-as-long-as-ive-got-you-lyrics" rel="noopener" data-api_path="/songs/279344">“As Long as I’ve Got You”</a>:</p>

<p></p><div class="embedly_preview embedly_preview--video">
<iframe type="text/html" width="640" height="390" frameborder="0" allowfullscreen="1" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/gp9uZjPaB4w?modestbranding=1&amp;start=18&amp;showinfo=0&amp;enablejsapi=1&amp;origin=genius.com"></iframe>
</div>

<p>The classic keys sample that can be heard throughout the beat was also taken from the previously mentioned song:</p>

<p></p><div class="embedly_preview embedly_preview--video">
<iframe type="text/html" width="640" height="390" frameborder="0" allowfullscreen="1" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/gp9uZjPaB4w?modestbranding=1&amp;start=0&amp;showinfo=0&amp;enablejsapi=1&amp;origin=genius.com"></iframe>
</div>
  </div>


</li>

    
      <li  class="question question--bottom_border ">
  <div class="u-bottom_margin">
    <h3 class="annotation_label">What has Method Man said about the song?</h3>
  </div>
  
  <div class="rich_text_formatting rich_text_formatting--no_vertical_margins">
    <p>Meth <a href="https://www.complex.com/music/2011/10/method-man-25-essential-songs/wu-tang-clan-cream-1993" rel="noopener nofollow">told <em>Complex</em></a>,</p>

<blockquote>
<p>‘C.R.E.A.M.’ was the one that really put us on the map if you wanna be technical. I wasn’t there when they recorded ‘C.R.E.A.M.’ I came in after the fact. RZA was like, ‘Put a hook on this song’ and I put a hook on it. That’s how it always went. I liked doing hooks.</p>

<p>The hook for that was done by my man Raider Ruckus. We used to work at the Statue of Liberty and when we were coming home we used to come up with all these made-up words that were acronyms.</p>

<p>We had words like ‘BIBWAM’ which meant, ‘Bitches Is Busted Without A Man’ and all this other crazy shit. Raider Ruckus was so ill with the way he put the words together. We would call money ‘cream’ so he took each letter and made a word out of it and killed it the way he did it.</p>

<p>Something like that had never been done before as far as a hook or even a way of speaking. This is just showing and proving that we paid attention in class when we was kids. You can’t do shit like that unless you got a brain in your fucking head! You got to have some level of intelligence to do something like that.</p>

<p>The best acronym for a word that I heard was ‘P.R.O.J.E.C.T.S.’ by Killah Priest. He said ‘People Relying On Just Enough Cash To Survive.’ And he’s the one that came up with ‘Basic Instructions Before Leaving Earth,’ the acronym for B.I.B.L.E. This ain’t no fluke shit man.</p>

<p>There’s a reason you got millions upon millions of fucking kids running around with Wu-Tang tattoos. You don’t just put something on your body permanently unless it’s official. At that time, when you’re coming out brand new and representing where you come from, everybody from that area wants you to win because they win. That’s what it was like for us.</p>

<p>We were the only dudes from Staten Island doing it so everybody from Staten Island wanted us to win. Not just dudes from Staten Island, but dudes from Brooklyn too because they had peoples in the group too. Then it was just grimy niggas who loved to see real shit, saying, ‘We riding with them Wu-Tang niggas. Fuck all that shiny suit shit!’ That ain’t no take on Puff, a lot of niggas was wearing suits and shit man, but that ain’t us.</p>
</blockquote>
  </div>


</li>

    
    
  </ul>
</div>
